  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

              <div id="descriptionmodule" class="module toggle-wrap">
               <div id="descriptionmodule_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>
                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>If a collection gets reloaded, then a core's isReloaded flag is always true. If a core experiences a ZK session expiration after a reload, then it won't ever be able to set itself to active because of the check in <tt>ZkController#register</tt>:</p> 
                  <div class="code panel" style="border-width: 1px;">
                   <div class="codeContent panelContent"> 
                    <pre class="code-java">        UpdateLog ulog = core.getUpdateHandler().getUpdateLog();
        <span class="code-keyword">if</span> (!core.isReloaded() &amp;&amp; ulog != <span class="code-keyword">null</span>) {
          <span class="code-comment">// disable recovery in <span class="code-keyword">case</span> shard is in construction state (<span class="code-keyword">for</span> shard splits)
</span>          Slice slice = getClusterState().getSlice(collection, shardId);
          <span class="code-keyword">if</span> (slice.getState() != Slice.State.CONSTRUCTION || !isLeader) {
            Future&lt;UpdateLog.RecoveryInfo&gt; recoveryFuture = core.getUpdateHandler().getUpdateLog().recoverFromLog();
            <span class="code-keyword">if</span> (recoveryFuture != <span class="code-keyword">null</span>) {
              log.info(<span class="code-quote">"Replaying tlog <span class="code-keyword">for</span> "</span> + ourUrl + <span class="code-quote">" during startup... NOTE: This can take a <span class="code-keyword">while</span>."</span>);
              recoveryFuture.get(); <span class="code-comment">// NOTE: <span class="code-keyword">this</span> could potentially block <span class="code-keyword">for</span>
</span>              <span class="code-comment">// minutes or more!
</span>              <span class="code-comment">// TODO: <span class="code-keyword">public</span> as recovering in the mean time?
</span>              <span class="code-comment">// TODO: in the <span class="code-keyword">future</span> we could <span class="code-keyword">do</span> peersync in parallel with recoverFromLog
</span>            } <span class="code-keyword">else</span> {
              log.info(<span class="code-quote">"No LogReplay needed <span class="code-keyword">for</span> core="</span> + core.getName() + <span class="code-quote">" baseURL="</span> + baseUrl);
            }
          }
          <span class="code-object">boolean</span> didRecovery = checkRecovery(coreName, desc, recoverReloadedCores, isLeader, cloudDesc,
              collection, coreZkNodeName, shardId, leaderProps, core, cc);
          <span class="code-keyword">if</span> (!didRecovery) {
            publish(desc, ZkStateReader.ACTIVE);
          }
        }
</pre> 
                   </div>
                  </div> 
                  <p>I can easily simulate this on trunk by doing:</p> 
                  <div class="code panel" style="border-width: 1px;">
                   <div class="codeContent panelContent"> 
                    <pre class="code-java">bin/solr -c -z localhost:2181
bin/solr create -c foo
bin/post -c foo example/exampledocs/*.xml
curl <span class="code-quote">"http:<span class="code-comment">//localhost:8983/solr/admin/collections?action=RELOAD&amp;name=foo"</span>
</span>kill -STOP &lt;PID&gt; &amp;&amp; sleep &lt;PAUSE_SECONDS&gt; &amp;&amp; kill -CONT &lt;PID&gt;
</pre> 
                   </div>
                  </div> 
                  <p>Where &lt;PID&gt; is the process ID of the Solr node. Here are the logs after the CONT command. As you can see below, the core never gets to setting itself as active again. I think the bug is that the isReloaded flag needs to get set back to false once the reload is successful, but I don't understand what this flag is needed for anyway???</p> 
                  <div class="code panel" style="border-width: 1px;">
                   <div class="codeContent panelContent">

INFO  - 2015-04-01 17:28:50.963; org.apache.solr.common.cloud.ConnectionManager; zkClient has disconnected

\u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eThanks for digging that up. I still don\'t understand why we have to keep track of whether a core has ever been reloaded as part of the long term state of a core. Using a flag to decide that we don\'t need to replay the tlog after a reload, while the reloaded core is initializing is one thing, but what\'s the point of remembering core A has been reloaded at some point in the past after core A has fully initialized and become active? I guess my point is it seems like a temporary state and not part of the long term state of a core. But that\'s orthogonal to this issue anyway, so I\'ll fix the register code and add a test for this.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"thelabdude\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_14391329_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=thelabdude\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"thelabdude\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Timothy Potter\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_14391329_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'01\\/Apr\\/15 19:57\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2015-04-01T19:57:53+0000\'\u003e01\\/Apr\\/15 19:57\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Thanks for digging that up. I still don\'t understand why we have to keep track of whether a core has ever been reloaded as part of the long term state of a core. Using a flag to decide that we don\'t need to replay the tlog after a reload, while the reloaded core is initializing is one thing, but what\'s the point of remembering core A has been reloaded at some point in the past after core A has fully initialized and become active? I guess my point is it seems like a temporary state and not part of the long term state of a core. But that\'s orthogonal to this issue anyway, so I\'ll fix the register code and add a test for this.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n
